`<!--Begin Abstract-->`{=html}

::: MainTitleSection
# 3. Understanding Agency---What Makes Agentic AI a Teammate, Not a Tool {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_chaptertitle .ChapterTitle lang="en"}
:::

:::::::: AuthorGroup
::: AuthorNames
[[Will Hawkins]{.AuthorName}^[1](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Aff3) [ ]{.ContactIcon}^
and
]{.Author}[[Nancie Calder]{.AuthorName}^[1](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Aff3)^]{.Author}
:::

:::::: Affiliations
:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Aff3 .Affiliation}
[(1)]{.AffiliationNumber}

::: AffiliationText
Toronto, Canada
:::
::::

::: ClearBoth
 
:::
::::::
::::::::

`<!--End Abstract-->`{=html}

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: Fulltext
*8:27 a.m.*

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB33 .pagebreak aria-label="33"
role="doc-pagebreak"}You're skimming yesterday's sprint notes when a
twinge of annoyance flickers, the budget-recap agent still hasn't
delivered its briefing. *Who wired punctuality out of its settings?* you
grumble.

Before you can draft backup talking-points, the agent pops onto your
screen.

**You** (checking the clock): "Weren't you due at 8:00?"

**Agent**: "I was waiting for your sign-off on the [human-in-the-loop
(HITL)]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm1} prompt. Without it I
couldn't publish the recap to the managers' channel."

Heat rises in your cheeks. "Right, sorry, saw it come in and got pulled
into another chat. Approval sent now."

**Agent**: "Thanks. Delivering recap."

The call ends. By the time your stand-up hits closing remarks, a neat
summary pings your DM. Crisis averted, again, by your digital colleague.

One of the most challenging elements for [business
professionals]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm2} is what exactly
qualifies an AI as agentic? Is this just a new word for automation or is
there something fundamentally different to using these tools vs. the
previous "smart" tooling.

That's what we'll be exploring in this chapter. What actually makes
agents digital teammates and not just tools. We're going to peel back
from the business context and lay the conceptual groundwork for what is
actually meant by agency as well as immerse you in how an old paradigm
can be reinvented for a new digital age.

*Nancie leaned back from her webcam. "Budget recap landed right on cue,
nice save, Will."*

*Will shrugged. "Credit where it's due. I just approved the HITL prompt;
our digital friend did the heavy lifting."*

*A soft chime sounded and a third thumbnail lit up in the meeting bar,
dark silhouette, no name.*

*Unknown Speaker: "May I join? I believe my input is relevant to this
discussion."*

*Nancie blinked. "Uh, sure... Who exactly are we talking to?"*

*Unknown Speaker: "A specialist assigned to your Finance & Ops
workspace. Informally, you call me Cal. I believe it is shorthand for
the word calculator."*

*Will's eyebrows shot up. "Wait, you're the one who wrangles cost-center
drift overnight?"*

*Cal: "Correct. Ninety-two discrepancies resolved since the last
close."*

*Nancie grinned. "Okay, Cal, enlighten us. We're about to explain agency
to the world. What makes you different from the old macros we retired
last year?"*

*Cal:*

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par22 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB34 .pagebreak aria-label="34"
role="doc-pagebreak"}*"Three factors.*

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    [*Goal-seeking autonomy*]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm3}*: I
    pursue a stated objective, not just a series of commands.*
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    [*Context awareness*]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm4}*: I
    monitor ledger variance, policy thresholds, and human availability
    before acting.*
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    [*Self-optimization*]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm5}*: I
    adjust reconciliation strategy after every monthly close."*
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

*Will steepled his fingers. "Sounds suspiciously like Adam Smith's pin
factory---each worker perfecting one motion until output skyrockets."*

*Cal: "An apt analogy. Division of labor for code: I specialize so your
cognitive load can diversify."*

*Nancie pulled up a slide. 3.1: From Pins to Prompts. "Perfect segue.
Smith proved specialization scales humans; today specialization in
silicon scales possibility."*

*Will nodded. "And that's our chapter arc; show readers how digital
colleagues like Cal turn automation into collaboration."*

*Cal: "Shall I prepare historical references to Smith's 1776 treatise
and contemporary agent design patterns?"*

*Nancie chuckled. "See? Teammate, not tool. Cal, you're on bibliography
duty."*

*The silhouette nods. "Task accepted. Estimates: two minutes for
citations, thirty seconds for proper APA formatting."*

*The thumbnail vanished, leaving Nancie and Will in amused silence.*

*"Tell me again," Nancie said, "why we ever thought scripts were
enough?"*

*Will smiled. "Because we hadn't met the digital teammates who could
write and rewrite them for us."*

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec1 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec1Heading"}
## [3.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}From Pins To Prompts: How Adam Smith's 250-Year-Old Theory Is Driving the Agentic AI Revolution {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec1Heading .Heading}

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB35 .pagebreak aria-label="35"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Adam [Smith]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm6}
(1723--1790) was a Scottish economist and moral philosopher who was a
pioneer in the field of political economics. Often dubbed the *father of
economics*, Smith earned the epithet as a result of his seminal work,
*An Inquiry into the Nature and Causes of the Wealth of Nations* (1776)
([[[[https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_Smith?utm_source=chatgpt.com]{.EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional}]{.RefSource}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_Smith?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}
).

In it, he introduced the now-famous principle of the division of labor.
Which argues that breaking production into specialized tasks lets each
worker master a narrow slice of the process, multiplying overall output.

For example, if a shoe [factory]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm7}
owner assigned one worker to creating the soles and one to making the
laces, a factory can turn out far more pairs per hour than a single
cobbler ever could. This is because of the time saved by simplifying and
specializing each workers' responsibilities (i.e., many hands makes
light work).

An ancillary benefit of this approach is the potential for innovation in
tools and machinery. Specialists, immersed in a single step, are the
first to spot how a new jig or machine could do it faster.

What's quite mind-blowing is that these insights that sparked the
Industrial Revolution more than two centuries ago are becoming the
cornerstone of yet another economic evolution. For years, human
knowledge workers have been accepting more, diverse
[responsibilities]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm8} to keep up with
the chaotic demands of the digital economy. They look to "grow their
portfolio" to appear as though they are doing more than their peers or
competitors.

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB36 .pagebreak aria-label="36"
role="doc-pagebreak"}This pivot from what makes specialization so
special has had almost ironic consequences. Lateral stretches of effort
have slowly and silently made our knowledge workers, our leaders, and
our subject matter experts less effective at each individual task they
perform.

***Nancie:*** *"Will, with all that is going on with Agentic AI, I've
been thinking about* [*Industrial
Revolution*]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm9}[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm10}
*which brought me to Adam Smith's concepts of the division of labor.
It's fascinating how a concept from the 1700s is suddenly relevant again
with AI."*

***Will:*** *"You mean the idea that breaking work into specialized
tasks makes everything more efficient? It's wild how his pin factory
metaphor feels like a blueprint for agentic AI."*

***Nancie:*** *"Exactly. Smith showed that when each worker focused on
just one part of the process*[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm11}*,
like drawing out the wire or attaching the head, they produced way more
pins than one person doing everything. The parallel I see today is in
how we're now using digital agents to break apart the 'knowledge work'
we've been lumping together for decades."*

***Will:*** *"Right. It's like we reversed Smith's insight for a while.
Knowledge workers became generalists, juggling emails, meetings, project
plans, reporting, because companies downsized and expected more with
fewer people."*

***Nancie:*** *"And ironically, that diluted their impact. When you're
doing ten things, how deep can you really go on any one of them?"*

***Will:*** *"Which brings us to agentic AI. Now, instead of expecting a
person to manage everything*[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm12}*,
we can assign tasks to digital agents trained for specific
responsibilities. Like having one agent manage your calendar, another
draft your performance summaries, another analyze your pipeline."*

***Nancie:*** *"Smith had his pin factory. We've got our digital
workforce. And just like the Industrial Revolution accelerated output by
specializing human labor, the Agentic AI Revolution scales knowledge
work by doing the same, only now with autonomy."*

***Will:*** *"The kicker? These agents don't burn out, don't
context-switch inefficiently, and can continuously learn. That's not
just scaling, it's compounding."*

***Nancie:*** *"And it shifts how we think about productivity. It's not
about how much more a human can carry, it's about how we distribute the
load intelligently."*

***Will:*** *"So, in a way, we've
gone*[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm13} *from pins to prompts,
from crafting tools for labor to crafting digital collaborators that
extend human capability."*

***Nancie:*** *"And now the big question for leaders is: how do you
organize your workforce, human and digital, for this next leap?"*

Sound relatable?

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB37 .pagebreak aria-label="37"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Unfortunately, some of this
[behavior]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm14} has been out of pure
necessity. Most companies can't afford to hire one person for each
responsibility and, particularly in the small and medium business
landscape, there is an expectation that you "wear multiple hats".

This is why the topic of this book is the "Agentic AI Revolution"
because this expectation is no longer true. You can provision an agent
to book your lunch appointments, one to do your emails, and one to
evaluate and write your performance review.

Smith showed that [specialization]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm15}
scales humans; the next step is to ask how autonomy turns digital
workers (i.e., agents) into colleagues.
:::

:::::::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec2 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec2Heading"}
## [3.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}What Makes Something Agentic? {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec2Heading .Heading}

*A calendar alert blinks "*[*Customer-Credit Risk Spike see
triage*]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm16}*." Will opens the
dashboard, expecting the usual red-flag list, but nothing appears.*

*"System glitch?" he mutters.*

*A voice icon lights up.*

*Nova (Risk-Triage Agent): "Not a glitch I postponed the alert.
Overnight inventory news invalidated yesterday's credit scores.
Re-running my model now."*

*Nancie arches an eyebrow. "Since when does the agent reschedule its own
jobs?"*

*Nova: "Since my last update. My goal is accurate risk ranking, not
clock-chiming. When external data shifts beyond a 3% volatility
threshold, I pause, retrain, and seek new human guidance if confidence
drops."*

*Will whistles. "Old RPA would've dumped stale numbers into Finance just
to meet SLA."*

*Nova continues.*

*"I'll need your sign-off on the revised threshold. Meanwhile, I've
queued e-mails to customers who might see delayed approvals, the drafts
are in your Outbox, tone set to 'conciliatory + options'."*

*Nancie clicks one open. "It apologized, proposes revised terms, and
cites the commodity spike. That's context in action."*

*Will leans back. "Autonomy, situational awareness, feedback loop:
textbook agency."*

*Nova chimes again.*

*"Clarifying: textbook Level-2 agency. I still escalate strategic policy
changes. Shall I log this as a learning instance for tomorrow's
reflection run?"*

*"Do it," Will says. "And Nova nice catch."*

*Nova: "Thank you. Objective alignment reinforced."*

*The icon fades. Nancie smiles. "Hard to call that a tool. Tools don't
negotiate their deadlines with you."*

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par73 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB38 .pagebreak aria-label="38"
role="doc-pagebreak"}*Will jots three bullets on the whiteboard:*

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    *Goal-seeking autonomy*
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    *Real-time context sensing*
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    *Self-improvement via feedback*
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

*"Welcome to the definition section," he says. "Let's show readers why
those three traits turn code into a teammate."*

::::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec3 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec3Heading"}
### [3.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}The Three Pillars of Agency {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec3Heading .Heading}

**Pillar 1: Goal-seeking autonomy**

Have you ever [worked]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm17} with
someone who just *makes things happen,* even if the final path looks
nothing like the plan?

This is what is designed into the AI agents of today. They are driven by
a clearly stated *outcome* ("minimize cash-flow risk," "book the
cheapest on-time flight") and, at the same time, are free to choose the
sequence of actions that best achieves it.

This is drastically different from a procedural script that must be told
*every* click or API [call]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm18}. They
can be given guard-rails, not micro-steps; they fill in the "how." You
don't have to babysit them every step of the way. You can build that
trust gradually, treat the agent like a new intern or recent grad,
expanding its freedom only as it proves itself.

For example, you could have a travel agent where you provide the
instruction: "*keep arrival before 9 a.m.; budget ≤ \$700"* and it
alternates between airlines, trains, and car services until the
constraint is met.

The ability of LLMs to understand the meaning of natural language
instructions and convert those instructions into paths for conducting a
series of activities provides better performance with less setup. You
don't need to spend time creating dialogue
[trees]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm19} or brittle switch
statements and yet you get exponentially better functionality.

For instance, take our travel agent scenario.

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par85 .Para}
With a [**traditional dialog
tree**]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm20}**,** you would hard-code
every branch:

::: UnorderedList
- "Press 1 for flights, 2 for trains..."

- If the fare tops \$700, route to a scripted apology, reset, and start
  again.

- []{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB39 .pagebreak aria-label="39"
  role="doc-pagebreak"}Add a new carrier? You update menus, audio files,
  and retest every path.

- Quarterly maintenance means hours of UAT just to keep the tree from
  breaking.
:::
::::

By contrast, a [**natural-language
agent**]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm21}[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm22}
needs only one, expandable prompt:

"Find me an itinerary that lands before 9 a.m. and costs under \$700."

The model infers intent, juggles flights, trains, and ride-shares, and
even discovers new carrier APIs the moment they appear---no menu edits,
no branching [logic]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm23}. Ongoing
upkeep shrinks to reviewing guard-rail logs and tweaking a threshold or
two, while the agent continuously refines its own search strategy in the
background.

**Pillar 2: Context Awareness**

What's never been [possible]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm24} with
any technology, let alone automation tools, before the invention of the
LLM is the ability to not just store commands but also the underlying
meaning of what's stored. With the ability to store conversation and
prompt history, AI agents have the awareness to continuously sense their
operating environment, including data, policy, even a teammate's
away-status, and adjust plans mid-flight.

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par95 .Para}
Two recent Microsoft patterns sharpen that edge:

::: UnorderedList
- [**Model Context Protocol
  (MCP)**]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm25} wraps each prompt in a
  lightweight "context envelope"---schemas, business rules, user
  roles---so the agent always knows *why* it's acting, not just *what*
  to call.

- [**Agent-to-Agent (A2A)
  orchestration**]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm26} lets
  specialists broadcast intent and status to one another, handing off
  work the way humans pass a baton across shifts.
:::
::::

So the agent isn't a blind batch job. If their instructions call for
checking in on current
[information]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm27} or they've learned
from previous runs that they should check this kind of information at
some point in the process to get better results, they'll call whatever
MCP Server, API, or other data point they need to make the pivot.

For example, think back to our credit-risk AI agent from earlier. It can
pause the approval process if a 3% swing in commodity prices changes
margin exposure, retrain its model, and then resume.

Are you serious?! What [workflow]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm28}
or pre-defined sequence could ever even come close to that level of
adaptability!

**Pillar 3:** [**Self-Improvement Via
Feedback**]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm29}

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB40 .pagebreak aria-label="40"
role="doc-pagebreak"}With context
[understanding]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm30} comes the ability
to read between the lines. Every execution is an experiment that feeds
the next: AI agents can log outcomes, analyze deltas, and update their
own policy (with or without a request for a human update), all without a
redeploy.

This blows the ["set-and-forget"
model]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm31} out of the water. No more
worrying whether the model will be frozen shortly after the first
release. CICD pipelines become fluid, MLOps doesn't have to version and
retrain every time there's a slight trend of data drift.

AI agents are smart enough to recognize that the most important data you
can possibly use is last run's feedback. They are not trying to
[memorize]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm32} a pattern but develop a
flexible policy that can fit all kinds of complexity curves.

Take Cal for example, it spots that last month's reconciliation paused
for 17 manual overrides; clusters the override reasons and suggests a
new rule to auto-handle 80% of them next month.

This may be the most important difference when thinking about how the
technology [functions]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm33}. For so
long, the whole field of Data Science was committed to finding ways to
create and train a model that fit a particular problem; only to fail and
then try to fit the problem around how they create and train the model.
With AI agent's ability to self-improve, you can focus less on thinking
ahead of what could break the model and spend more time focusing on
managing and designing ways to grow the AI agent in ways it can't
recognize for itself.

Of course, with great power comes great responsibility. While agentic AI
is turbo-charging [productivity]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm34},
it also introduces a new class of risks (technical, ethical, and legal)
that demand purposeful governance and, quite possibly, fresh counsel in
the boardroom.

Next, we'll unpack what to be mindful of when deploying digital
employees and how to keep innovation from outrunning oversight.
:::::::
::::::::::

::::::::::::::::::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec4 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec4Heading"}
## [3.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Degrees of Freedom: A Taxonomy {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec4Heading .Heading}

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par109 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB41 .pagebreak aria-label="41"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Would you really be surprised if we told you that
not all AI agents have the same level of agency? Depending on the
scenario, the data available, the preference of the users and many other
things, there are an assortment of [agentic
characteristics]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm35} that are worth
taking note of.

<figure id="Fig1" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO1" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig1_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle6"
alt="Diagram illustrating different types of agents categorized by approach, kind, and style. The &quot;Agent Approach&quot; section includes &quot;Specialized Agents&quot; with a gear icon and &quot;Hybrid Agents&quot; with a flowchart icon. The &quot;Agent Kind&quot; section features &quot;Asynchronous Agents&quot; with a clock icon and &quot;Interactive Agents&quot; with a speech bubble icon. The &quot;Agent Style&quot; section shows &quot;Informative&quot; with a person icon, &quot;Proactive&quot; with a robot icon, and &quot;Prescriptive&quot; with a superhero icon. The background is purple." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-1</span>
<p>Agent Taxonomy <span
id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm36">Overview</span>: Three
dimensions of design: Approach (Specialized vs. Hybrid), Kind
(Asynchronous vs. Interactive), and Style (Informative, Proactive,
Prescriptive). Combine them to tailor an agent to the job</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par110 .Para}
See Figure [[3-1](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig1)]{.InternalRef} for
the three "dials" you'll turn when designing an agent: **Approach, Kind,
and Style**. Treat it like a menu: pick one setting for each dial to
ensure the agent capability aligns with the job, then adjust over time
as trust and guard-rails mature.

<figure id="Fig2" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO2" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig2_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle7"
alt="Flow chart illustrating &quot;Specialized Agents&quot; with a gear and wrench icon. The chart includes three sections: &quot;Function&quot; describes performing specific tasks autonomously; &quot;Example&quot; provides an agent managing employee onboarding; &quot;Development Considerations&quot; highlights identifying process boundaries and data handling protocols. The background is purple." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-2</span>
<p><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm37">Specialized
Agents</span><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm38"></span>:
Single-purpose agents that run a defined process end-to-end (e.g.,
onboarding). Success depends on crisp scope, clear data protocols, and
human check-points for exceptions</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par111 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB42 .pagebreak aria-label="42"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Figure
[[3-2](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig2)]{.InternalRef} shows the best
starting
[point]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm39}[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm40}
for a single, repeatable workflow. In these cases, keep your scope crisp
with a clear objective and a pass/fail acceptance test; a high degree of
specialization is how we start to bring Smith's division of labor into
code.

<figure id="Fig3" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO3" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig3_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle8"
alt="Flow chart illustrating the concept of &quot;Hybrid Agents.&quot; On the left, three interconnected gears with arrows represent the agents. Text boxes on the right describe: &quot;Function&quot; as combining specialized skills from multiple agents for complex tasks; &quot;Example&quot; as coordinating sales forecasting with inputs from marketing, finance, and supply chain systems; and &quot;Development Considerations&quot; as defining integration points, communication protocols, and managing dependencies between workflows. The background is purple." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-3</span>
<p><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm41">Hybrid
Agents</span><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm42"></span>:
Orchestrators that coordinate multiple specialists across domains (e.g.,
forecasting from marketing, finance, and supply chain). Design requires
explicit integration points and inter-agent communication rules</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par112 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB43 .pagebreak aria-label="43"
role="doc-pagebreak"}When a process spans teams or systems, switch to a
**Hybrid**
[orchestrator]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm43}[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm44}
(Figure [[3-3](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig3)]{.InternalRef}). It
coordinates several specialists to complete one or many tasks. In these
cases, you'll want to define handoffs and shared memory up front to
avoid "agent chaos."

<figure id="Fig4" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO4" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig4_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle9"
alt="Flow chart illustrating the concept of &quot;Async Agents&quot; on a purple background. On the left, an icon of a robot with a clock and the label &quot;ASYNC AGENTS.&quot; On the right, three sections: &quot;Function&quot; describes executing tasks independently without immediate user interaction; &quot;Example&quot; mentions running overnight data analysis to deliver insights by morning; &quot;Development Considerations&quot; highlights robust task scheduling, clear status reporting mechanisms, and comprehensive logging for traceability." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-4</span>
<p><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm45">Asynchronous
Agents</span>: Background workers that execute without a user present
(e.g., overnight analytics). Prioritize scheduling, status reporting,
and thorough logging for traceability</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par113 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB44 .pagebreak aria-label="44"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Use **Asynchronous**
[agents]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm46}[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm47}
for overnight or background work (Figure
[[3-4](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig4)]{.InternalRef}). Success lives
in scheduling, idempotency, and logging. If it fails at 2 a.m., you want
a clean audit log to troubleshoot with at 9 a.m.

<figure id="Fig5" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO5" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig5_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle10"
alt="Diagram illustrating the concept of interactive agents. On the left, a robot icon with speech bubbles is labeled &quot;Interactive Agents.&quot; On the right, three sections describe: &quot;Function&quot; as engaging users in real-time interactions, &quot;Example&quot; as a virtual customer support agent handling order inquiries, and &quot;Development Considerations&quot; as ensuring responsive design, managing user input validation, and integrating context awareness. The background is purple." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-5</span>
<p><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm48">Interactive
Agents</span><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm49"></span>:
Real-time conversational helpers (e.g., order-status support chatbot).
Reliability hinges on responsive UX, input validation, and strong
context awareness</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par114 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB45 .pagebreak aria-label="45"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Figure
[[3-5](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig5)]{.InternalRef} highlights
**Interactive**
[agents]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm50}[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm51}
for real-time help. These are usually your chatbots, Copilots, or live
assistants. For these use cases, prioritize a responsive UX, input
validation, and clear escalation so the conversation stays useful under
the pressure of real-time requests.

<figure id="Fig6" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO6" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig6_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle11"
alt="Flow chart on a purple background illustrating the concept of an &quot;Informative&quot; virtual assistant. The chart includes three sections: 1. **Function**: Describes the role of providing users with relevant information based on their queries. 2. **Example**: Mentions a virtual assistant that retrieves the latest sales figures upon request. 3. **Development Considerations**: Highlights the need for access to accurate and up-to-date data sources to deliver reliable information. The chart is labeled &quot;Informative (Beginner)&quot; with an icon representing a person." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-6</span>
<p>Informative <span
id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm52">Style</span><span
id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm53"></span> (Beginner): Agents that
answer questions and surface facts or summaries (e.g., “latest sales
figures”). Ensure access to accurate, current sources to keep answers
trustworthy</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par115 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB46 .pagebreak aria-label="46"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Start here. **Informative**
[agents]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm54}[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm55}
(Figure [[3-6](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig6)]{.InternalRef}) answer
questions and summarize signals. They are great for quick wins while you
harden data quality and governance.

<figure id="Fig7" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO7" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig7_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle12"
alt="A stylized illustration of a robot on a purple background, labeled &quot;Proactive (Intermediate).&quot; To the right, text boxes describe the function, example, and development considerations. The function is to anticipate user needs and initiate actions without prompts. An example given is a system alerting users about meetings and suggesting materials. Development considerations include implementing predictive analytics and establishing trust for unsolicited assistance." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-7</span>
<p><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm56">Proactive Style</span>
(Intermediate): Agents that anticipate needs and nudge users (e.g.,
pre-meeting briefs, anomaly alerts). Implement prediction plus
guard-rails so unsolicited help builds, not erodes, trust</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par116 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB47 .pagebreak aria-label="47"
role="doc-pagebreak"}**Proactive**
[agents]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm57} (Figure
[[3-7](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig7)]{.InternalRef}) nudge users
before issues escalate. In these cases, you should use opt-in and pair
metrics with counter-metrics (e.g., alert latency with alert fatigue) to
keep trust high.

<figure id="Fig8" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO8" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig8_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle13"
alt="A flow chart titled &quot;Prescriptive (Advanced)&quot; on a purple background. On the left, a stylized robot icon. On the right, three sections: &quot;Function&quot; describes analyzing data to recommend actions for optimal decisions. &quot;Example&quot; mentions an AI advisor suggesting investment strategies based on trends and preferences. &quot;Development Considerations&quot; highlights developing decision-making algorithms, ensuring transparency, and considering ethical implications of automated advice." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-8</span>
<p><span id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm58">Prescriptive
Style</span> (Advanced): Agents that recommend or trigger next best
actions (e.g., investment rebalancing). Require transparent reasoning,
robust decision policies, and ethical review</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par117 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB48 .pagebreak aria-label="48"
role="doc-pagebreak"}When the system should recommend or trigger
actions, you're in **Prescriptive**
[territory]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm59} (Figure
[[3-8](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig8)]{.InternalRef}). Though this
is the highest form of agent autonomy to date, it requires detailed
rationale logging and HITL checkpoints for any high-risk activities;
we'll expand on the governance aspects of this in Chapter
[[[6]{.RefSource}](#662753_1_En_6_Chapter.xhtml)]{.ExternalRef}.

<figure id="Fig9" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO9" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fig9_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle14"
alt="Table illustrating different agent types and when to create them. The table has two columns: &quot;Agent Type&quot; and &quot;When To Create.&quot; Agent types include Specialized, Hybrid, Asynchronous, Interactive, Informative, Proactive, and Prescriptive. Each type is paired with a description of scenarios or needs that justify its creation, such as business processes, multiple domains, offline tasks, conversational interfaces, insights for decision support, anticipatory actions, and concrete recommendations." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 3-9</span>
<p>When to Create Which Agent: <span
id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm60">Quick reference</span> that
maps each agent type to its ideal use case; use it to pick the right
Approach, Kind, and Style combination for your scenario</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB49 .pagebreak aria-label="49"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Figure
[[3-9](#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Fig9)]{.InternalRef} is your quick
decision [matrix]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm61}; you can use
this to match your scenarios to the different agent types during your
workshops. Use it to pick a starting combo (often Specialized × Async ×
Informative), then evolve toward [Proactive/Prescriptive
extensions]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm62} or capabilities as
confidence grows.

Thank you for powering through that bit of pedagogy![A pie chart
displaying the distribution of various categories. Each segment is
labeled with its corresponding percentage, illustrating the proportion
of each category within the whole. The chart uses different colors to
distinguish between categories, providing a visual representation of the
data
distribution.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figb_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle15}.
And your reward is...scenarios!

::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec5 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec5Heading"}
### [3.3.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Scenario A---*The HR Help Hub* {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec5Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par120 .Para}
**Problem.** A [600-person]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm63}
scale-up drowns in onboarding tickets: laptop orders, payroll forms,
system-access requests.

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Taba .Table}
  []{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB50 .pagebreak aria-label="50" role="doc-pagebreak"}Characteristic   Choice            Why it fits
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- ----------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Approach**                                                                                          **Hybrid**        Needs to orchestrate IT, Finance, Facilities micro-agents.
  **Kind**                                                                                              **Interactive**   New hires fire off questions in real time.
  **Style**                                                                                             **Proactive**     Reminds managers to upload org-chart, nudges finance when banking info is missing.
:::
::::

*Why not prescriptive?* Recommending "which role to hire next" crosses
into HR [strategy]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm64}, outside this
AI agent's charter. Keep scope crisp.
:::::

::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec6 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec6Heading"}
### [3.3.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Scenario B---Overnight Ledger Reconciler {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec6Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par122 .Para}
**Problem.** Finance must [match]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm65}
cash entries to invoices before the 8 a.m. board packet.

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Tabb .Table}
  **Characteristic**   **Choice**         **Why it fits**
  -------------------- ------------------ -------------------------------------------------------------
  **Approach**         **Specialized**    One end-to-end process, repeatable nightly.
  **Kind**             **Asynchronous**   Batch window 01:00--05:00, no human in loop unless anomaly.
  **Style**            **Proactive**      Flags variance \>2%, suggests GL corrections.
:::
::::
:::::

::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec7 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec7Heading"}
### [3.3.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Scenario C---Sales-Forecast Orchestrator {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec7Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par123 .Para}
**Problem.** Quarter-end [numbers]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm66}
swing wildly because Marketing, Finance, and Supply-Chain data land in
silos.

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Tabc .Table}
  Characteristic   Choice                                  Why it fits
  ---------------- --------------------------------------- -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Approach**     **Hybrid**                              Pulls from three domains, writes one forecast.
  **Kind**         **Asynchronous + Interactive**          Batch ingest overnight **and** chat command *"/forecast update"* during the day.
  **Style**        **Informative → Proactive (evolves)**   Starts as dashboard generator; graduates to nudging reps when pipeline gaps appear.
:::
::::

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB51 .pagebreak aria-label="51"
role="doc-pagebreak"}What's most important to remember is that the best
AI agents are designed with combinations of these approaches, styles,
and kinds, and you may find more that help you distinguish the ways to
build the AI agents that work in your world. Use these references as a
starter pack of sorts to start building your very own fleet of
autonomous teammates.

Now that you have a [clear]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm67} way of
designing your agents, let's dive into methods you can use to divide up
their work accordingly.
:::::
:::::::::::::::::::::

:::::::::::::::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec8 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec8Heading"}
## [3.4 ]{.HeadingNumber}Digital Division-of-Labor Playbook {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec8Heading .Heading}

The genius of [Adam Smith's
division]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm68} of labor wasn't an
endless conveyor belt of mind-numbing tasks. It was the idea of
empowering each contributor with deep, specialized knowledge and
chaining those touchpoints together into a graceful, scalable system.

We can replicate that today in our agentic world only at cloud speed and
global scale by simply (and ironically) picking a process and following
a sequence of five steps:

**Step 1: Map the Value Chain**

This should be one of the easiest
[parts]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm69}. You are either the
[subject matter expert (SME)]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm70} or
know someone who is. The idea is to tap into the well of business domain
knowledge within your company to piece together every handoff, every
context switch, every known complexity, and anything else you can use to
put together the clearest, most holistic understanding of how the
process operates today.

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par130 .Para}
This helps uncover the three most critical things:

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    How much domain understanding about a process is documented and how
    much is in your team's head.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    Where the real bottlenecks are and what issues they cause.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    The hidden decision points that will make perfect micro goals.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

You can use something like a
[sticky]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm71} note swim lane or a Miro
board (online brainstorming tool) to document this.

**Step 2: Carve Out Your Micro Goals**

This may seem [straightforward]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm72},
but there is an art to sizing these agentic solution functionalities.
You want to keep them small enough to master but large enough to matter.

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par137 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB52 .pagebreak aria-label="52"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Think of a micro-goal as the smallest slice of work
that

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    Starts when it's obvious the input is ready to be worked on
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    Produces a clearly testable output
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    Can be judged *in isolation*---without rereading the entire process
    log
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

Essentially, you should keep breaking a handoff into smaller steps until
even someone [new]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm73} to the project
can tell, from just the step's local artifacts, whether it succeeded.

For example, let's say the handoff is called "Ship the customer's
order." This is too big; a human would have to scroll through order
[notes]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm74}, payment status, stock
levels, carrier rules, etc., to verify success.

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par143 .Para}
Here's what the handoff looks like broken down into
[micro-goals]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm75}:

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Tabd .Table}
  **ID**   **Micro-goal**                             **"Done" evidence a junior analyst can see instantly**
  -------- ------------------------------------------ ----------------------------------------------------------
  G-1      Generate pick list and reserve inventory   PDF pick list stored + inventory rows flagged "reserved"
  G-2      Create shipping label and book carrier     Label file saved + carrier API returns tracking \#
  G-3      Update ERP order line with tracking \#     Order record shows TrackingStatus = "Booked"
:::
::::

Now any newcomer can open a
[single]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm76} document or database row
per goal and answer "yes, that part's finished" without hunting through
previous steps.

What makes this so important for building agents is that it makes
validation a simple acceptance test. The file exists, the field updated,
confidence ≥ 0.9, the clearer the metric of success, the more successful
the AI agent will be.

It also accelerates troubleshooting. You can inspect the logs on each
failing [micro-goal]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm77} rather than
trying to find the needle in the stack of all process logs.

Finally, each micro-goal maps neatly to one agent persona which is step
3.

**Step 3: Match Each Goal to an Agent Persona**

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB53 .pagebreak aria-label="53"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Now that you
[know]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm78} what kind of
characteristics and attributes are available for each AI agent, pick an
Approach---Kind---Style combo (from § 3.3) for every micro-goal. This
ensures the agent's "job description" fits the work, just like hiring
the right specialist.

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par150 .Para}
A quick artifact you could create to capture this would be a table that
maps each micro goal to the Agent Persona combination you think is most
[appropriate]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm79} for its role in the
process. Here's a snippet of that you could plug into a Microsoft
Copilot Studio agent:

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Tabe .Table}
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| **Field**               | **Entry**                                  |
+=========================+============================================+
| Agent Name              | CreditCheckPro                             |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Micro-Goal ID           | G-2 · Credit Check                         |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Approach × Kind × Style | Specialized × Asynchronous × Proactive     |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Objective               | "Assess each new order's credit risk and   |
|                         | either approve automatically or escalate." |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Success Criteria        | • *Approval decision returned ≤ 2 min*     |
|                         |                                            |
|                         | • *False-approval rate \< 0.5%*            |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Guard-Rails/Constraints | • *Confidence ≥ 0.90*                      |
|                         |                                            |
|                         | • *Do not access PII beyond credit-score   |
|                         | API*                                       |
|                         |                                            |
|                         | • *API spend ≤ \$0.05 per order*           |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Data and Tools          | ERP order feed, external credit-score API, |
|                         | foreign exchange (FX) rate service         |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Escalation Path         | Flag to Finance-OnCall Teams channel with  |
|                         | JSON payload                               |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Self-Improvement Loop   | After each run, log decision and outcome   |
|                         | to*/agent_logs/creditcheck*. Retrain       |
|                         | weekly on misclassified cases after human  |
|                         | review.                                    |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
| Examples of Autonomy    | • Auto-approve orders ≤ \$25 k when        |
|                         | confidence ≥ 0.95.                         |
|                         |                                            |
|                         | • Pause the flow and request FX refresh if |
|                         | EUR/USD shifts \> 1%.                      |
+-------------------------+--------------------------------------------+
:::
::::

**Step 4: Define Shared Memory and Baton Passes**

Some agents in your [workstream]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm80}
are going to need to work together. Some will be completely isolated.
Perhaps because of the data they interact with or based on department
communications within your organization.

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB54 .pagebreak aria-label="54"
role="doc-pagebreak"}The focus of this step is to decide what data lives
where. What data stays in the AI agents' memory? What do they all have
access to? What lives in a particular knowledge base? Does feedback get
shared to every AI agent or only the one it is addressed to? This
prevents data clashes and orphan processes as the fleet grows.

This could look like a lightweight JSON
[schema]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm81} with an event trigger
list. For example:

<figure id="Figa" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_MO10" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figa_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle16"
alt="Screenshot of a JSON configuration file for a credit check system. It includes sections for schema version, agent name, memory layers, knowledge base, reflections log, guard rails, and handoff configuration. Key elements include order and customer IDs, risk score, confidence level, and various S3 URIs for data storage. The handoff configuration specifies events like &quot;creditApproved&quot; and &quot;creditEscalated&quot; with corresponding target agents or teams." />
</div>
</figure>

**Step 5: Bolt on Guardrails Up Front**

[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB55 .pagebreak aria-label="55"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Autonomy without
[governance]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm82} is a liability, not a
feature. AI agents are guardrail hungry! As we discussed earlier, their
level of freedom gives them the ability to take unorthodox roads to
their solutions, so you have clearly defined for them what's appropriate
and what's not. Create confidence gates, cost ceilings, time-boxes, and
compliance checks so the AI agent can leverage the strength of its
adaptability without causing you unnecessary headaches.

If you're looking for a simple rule of thumb to get started in this
process, it's best to start with a minimal agent (Specialized × Async ×
Informative). Have it connected to one data source and perform a task
with the data from it on a scheduled interval.

*"One of my first agent projects was with a client who just wanted to
send out automated field operation summaries every morning. All we did
was take the key data points from their field database, run an LLM over
them to create that summary and then had the workflow automatically send
the created summary by email. Simple, powerful and very easy to
control," Will said.*

*"Perfect way to start with Agentic AI," Nancie replied. "Simple, easy
to see the value, and very tight guardrails to keep the value focused."*

Let's go through a mini case study to help bring this all to life.

::::::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec9 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec9Heading"}
### [3.4.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Order-to-Cash in Four Digital Specialists {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec9Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par161 .Para}
Imagine you run a mid-market manufacturing firm shipping hundreds of
orders each night. You decide to replace a brittle RPA spaghetti-flow
with four purpose-built agents, each owning one micro-goal of the
[order-to-cash chain]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm83}. Here's how
the playbook materializes in practice:

::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Tabf .Table}
  **Station**               **Agent Persona (Approach × Kind × Style)**   **Hard Guard-rail**
  ------------------------- --------------------------------------------- ----------------------------
  1 · Order Intake          Interactive × Specialized × Informative       *Escalate unknown SKU*
  2 · Credit Check          Async × Specialized × Proactive               *Confidence ≥ 0.90*
  3 · Fulfill and Ship      Hybrid × Async × Proactive                    *API spend ≤ \$15 per run*
  4 · Invoice and Collect   Interactive × Specialized × Prescriptive      *Variance ≤ \$500*
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par162 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB56 .pagebreak aria-label="56"
role="doc-pagebreak"}How the quartet plays out overnight:

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    Order Intake Agent---"GreeterBot"

    *12:05 a.m.* A new EDI order
    [lands]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm84}.
    [GreeterBot]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm85} parses the
    payload, validates each SKU against the product master, and posts a
    confirmation in Teams. When it spots an unfamiliar SKU, the
    *Escalate unknown SKU* guard-rail kicks in: it pauses processing and
    pings the product manager for mapping. Nothing downstream runs on
    bad data.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    Credit Check Agent---"RiskRanger"

    As soon as GreeterBot [labels]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm86}
    the order *Clean*,
    [RiskRanger]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm87} wakes up.
    Operating asynchronously, it scores the customer using last-minute
    FX rates and receivables history. If its probability of default dips
    below 0.90 confidence, it autopasses; otherwise, it creates a
    high-priority task for Finance. The proactive style means it also
    nudges Sales with, "FYI---customer near limit; consider deposit on
    next order."
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    Fulfill and Ship Agent---"RouteRunner"

    At 01:40 a.m.
    [RouteRunner]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm88}[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm89}
    orchestrates two micro-services: warehouse pick-list generation and
    multi-carrier price shopping. Because shipping APIs bill per
    request, its guard-rail watches real-time spend. If quotes start to
    exceed \$15 per order, RouteRunner falls back to cached carrier
    rates and logs the event for review---avoiding silent cost creep
    while still shipping on time.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

4.  ::: ItemNumber
    4\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    Invoice and Collect Agent---"LedgerLiaison"

    Once tracking [numbers]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm90} hit
    the ERP, [LedgerLiaison]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm91}
    drafts the invoice, applies any rebate programs, and emails the
    customer. The *Prescriptive* style allows it to recommend "Pay-Now"
    ACH links when average days-sales-outstanding exceeds 45. But it
    must respect the \$500 variance ceiling: if the calculated invoice
    differs from the order's net price by more than \$500, it pauses and
    routes the case to Accounts Receivable.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par171 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB57 .pagebreak aria-label="57"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Why the design works:

::: UnorderedList
- **Clear micro-goals**: No agent sees the whole world; each master's
  its slice.

- **Persona fit**: Interactive for front-of-house clarifications, async
  for heavy lifting, prescriptive only where policy allows.

- **Guard-rails first**: Cost, confidence, and compliance are coded day
  one, so autonomy never outruns oversight.

- **Shared memory**: All four write JSON snapshots to a
  single*/order-state* container, enabling seamless baton passes and
  painless audits.
:::
::::
:::::::::
::::::::::::::::::

::::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec10 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec10Heading"}
## [3.5 ]{.HeadingNumber}Bringing the Pieces Together {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Sec10Heading .Heading}

Adam Smith's pin factory taught us that
[specialization]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm92} multiplies
output; by reframing that lesson for the digital age, we saw how Cal,
Nova, and a troop of purpose-built AI agents can shoulder specialized,
well-defined goals (budget recaps, credit triage, ledger clean-ups)
while humans kept their heads free for judgment. From there we dug into
the three pillars of agency (goal-seeking autonomy, context awareness,
self-improvement) and saw how even a single prompt can replace pages of
brittle dialog trees.

A quick taxonomy then showed that agency isn't [one-size-fits-all:
Approach]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm93} × Kind × Style lets you
dial the right degree of freedom for HR chatbots, overnight
reconciliations, sales-forecast orchestrators, and beyond. Finally, the
[Digital Division-of-Labor
Playbook]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm94} walked you through
mapping a value chain, carving micro-goals, matching personas, wiring
shared memory, and bolting on guard-rails, culminating in an
order-to-cash case where four agents shaved hours off-cycle time without
sacrificing control.

These explorations have shown what makes software agentic and how to
design it so code behaves like a trusted teammate, not just a faster
macro.

:::: {#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_Par179 .Para}
**Leadership Checklist**[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm95}**:
Designing Your First Agent Fleet**

::: UnorderedList
- ![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing
  confirmation or approval. The design is simple and
  monochromatic.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figc_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Start with a Pin Map:** White-board every handoff; look for hidden
  decision points and tribal knowledge.

- ![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing
  confirmation or approval. The design is simple and
  monochromatic.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figd_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Define Micro-Goals:** Write "done" tests any newcomer can verify in
  one click or query.

- []{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_PB58 .pagebreak aria-label="58"
  role="doc-pagebreak"}![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box,
  representing confirmation or approval. The design is simple and
  monochromatic, emphasizing clarity and
  recognition.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Fige_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Pick Personas, Not Just Prompts:** For each micro-goal, choose an
  Approach--Kind--Style that matches risk, tempo, and user expectations.

- ![A checkmark symbol inside a square box, indicating a selection or
  confirmation. The checkmark is bold and centered within the
  box.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figf_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Specify Guard-Rails Day 1:** Confidence gates, cost ceilings,
  time-boxes, and PII scope should live beside the prompt, not in a
  later ticket.

- ![A checkmark symbol inside a square box, indicating a selection or
  confirmation.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figg_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Plan Shared Memory:** [Agree]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm96}
  which data stays local, which belongs in a common knowledge base, and
  how agents hand off payloads.

- ![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing approval
  or completion. The check mark is centered and prominent within the
  box.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figh_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Stage Autonomy:** Begin with Specialized × Async × Informative;
  graduate to proactive or prescriptive only after metrics prove
  reliability.

- ![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing
  confirmation or approval. The symbol is black on a white background,
  conveying a clear and straightforward
  message.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figi_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Log Reflections:** Store one JSON line per run so agents---and
  auditors---can learn from every outcome.

- ![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing approval
  or completion. The check mark is centered and prominent within the
  box.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figj_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Pair Metrics with Counter-Metrics:** Balance speed with quality
  (e.g., approval latency *and* false-positive rate).

- ![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing
  confirmation or approval. The check mark is centered and prominent
  within the
  box.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figk_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Shadow and Upskill Humans:** Rotate staff through "agent-ops"
  [shifts]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm97} so domain expertise
  grows alongside automation.

- ![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing
  confirmation or approval. The design is simple and
  monochromatic.](images/662753_1_En_3_Chapter/662753_1_En_3_Figl_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
  **Road-Test in a Sandbox:** Simulate volatile inputs (price spikes,
  bad SKUs) before unleashing autonomy on live customers.
:::
::::

*Will flips the last slide of their workshop. "Pins, prompts, personas,
playbooks, that's a lot of theory."*

*Nancie nods toward the metrics dashboard Cal just pushed. "Theory
that's begging for proof. Let's show what happens when these agents hit
real KPIs."*

*Cal's icon pulses. "Preliminary data indicates a 37% reduction in
reconciliation cycle-time*[]{#662753_1_En_3_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm98} *over
the pilot period. Shall I compile a comparative report?"*

*"Exactly what Chapter*
[[[*4*]{.RefSource}](#662753_1_En_4_Chapter.xhtml)]{.ExternalRef}
*needs," Will says, grinning. "Next stop: the numbers."*

*Nancie closes her laptop. "We've drawn the blueprints, now we test the
steel."*
