Orchestration, AI Service Suite, and Business Applications, with a
cross-cutting ribbon for governance, security, identity, and
observability. It illustrates how OneLake/Fabric, Agent
Service/Microsoft Agent Framework/models, and Power Automate/Dynamics
work together under Purview and Entra controls</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec2 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec2Heading"}
### [5.1.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}The Infrastructure Foundation (Figure [[5-1](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig1)]{.InternalRef}---Bottom Circle) {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec2Heading .Heading}

[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB77 .pagebreak aria-label="77"
role="doc-pagebreak"}This is the
[resilient]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm10}, scalable bedrock of
hardware, data centers, compute and storage capabilities that form the
sandbox where agents can access data, run safely, and scale to meet
demands of users and their business problems.

Azure's global network of hyper-scale data centers provides the
high-density GPU and FPGA clusters necessary to train and serve large
language and vision models at enterprise scale.

Virtual networks and private endpoints guard data in transit, while
[Azure's Advanced Data Residency
(ADR)]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm11} options let you keep data
and compute within chosen geographies for compliance. Role-based access,
encryption at rest and in motion, and
[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB78 .pagebreak aria-label="78"
role="doc-pagebreak"}identity-based controls ensure that only authorized
agents and humans can tap into sensitive sources. This gives any
technologist confidence that every call from Copilot or custom agents
[remains]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm12} within tightly
controlled boundaries.
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec3 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec3Heading"}
### [5.1.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Data and Orchestration (Figure [[5-1](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig1)]{.InternalRef}---Data Orchestration Circle) {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec3Heading .Heading}

Microsoft Fabric [sits]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm13} on top of
the raw infrastructure the way Microsoft 365 sits on top of Windows: a
fully managed, SaaS-style workbench that unifies every way your people
ingest, shape, secure, and serve data to agents.

Onelake's Delta Parquet storage format writes any dataset under a
standard format producing the ability for a single source of truth
across various disparate data sources. This means agents always learn
from the most recent, consistent view of business and operational
information.

On top of OneLake, Fabric [layers]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm14}
a lakehouse/warehouse duo that replaces the sprawl of separate Spark,
SQL, and BI silos. Lakehouse serves data-engineering capabilities, while
the Warehouse workload provides a Synapse-compatible SQL surface
complete with row-level security and forthcoming audit logs for analysts
and LLM agents that prefer ANSI SQL.

[Data movement]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm15} is handled by Data
Factory in Fabric, whose Dataflow Gen2 and PySpark notebooks and
pipelines bring self-service, Copilot-assisted ETL transformations,
CI/CD, and Git integration into the same workspace where your Lakehouse
lives.

This all combines as a [business]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm16}
user-oriented platform that ensures all agents drink from, and
contribute back to, the same, ever-fresh data lake.
:::

::::::::::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec4 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec4Heading"}
### [5.1.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}AI Service Suite (Figure [[5-1](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig1)]{.InternalRef}---AI Service Suite Circle) {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec4Heading .Heading}

This third [layer]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm17} is designed as
a multipersona workbench for converting agent concepts into running
code. Azure AI Agent Service, Azure OpenAI and Cognitive Services,
Copilot Studio, and the open-source Microsoft Agent Framework together
form a workbench that lets every persona, from pro-dev to citizen maker,
design, refine, and operate autonomous agents.

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec5 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec5Heading"}
#### Azure AI Agent Service---Managed Runtime and Orchestration {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec5Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par22 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB79 .pagebreak aria-label="79"
role="doc-pagebreak"}[Azure AI Agent
Service]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm18}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm19}
is the managed engine that stitches models, tools, and memory stores
into a single, stateful runtime. It spins up conversation threads,
routes tool calls, persists agent memory, and enforces content-safety
and identity controls so solutions stay secure and scalable out of the
box ([[[Microsoft
Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/ai-foundry/agents/overview?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef},
[[[TECHCOMMUNITY.​MICROSOFT.​COM]{.RefSource}](https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/azure-ai-services-blog/introducing-azure-ai-agent-service/4298357?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).

::: UnorderedList
- **Built-in observability** streams metrics to Azure Monitor and the
  new Foundry Observability panel announced at Build 2025, which focuses
  on tracking agent-specific markers ([[[The Official Microsoft
  Blog]{.RefSource}](https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2025/05/19/microsoft-build-2025-the-age-of-ai-agents-and-building-the-open-agentic-web/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).

- **Pluggable memory** lets you swap Redis for Cosmos DB or Vector
  Search without changing the agent's code
  ([[[TECHCOMMUNITY.​MICROSOFT.​COM]{.RefSource}](https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/azure-ai-services-blog/announcing-general-availability-of-azure-ai-foundry-agent-service/4414352?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).
:::
::::

This engine is designed for Pro
[developers]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm20}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm21}
and ML engineers who need full control over code, CI/CD, and custom
toolchains.
:::::

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec6 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec6Heading"}
#### Microsoft Agent Framework---Unified SDK for Prompt Routing, Memory & Multi-Agent Workflows {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec6Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par26 .Para}
Sitting just
[above]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm22}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm23}
the runtime, **Microsoft Agent Framework** is the open-source SDK that
unifies and succeeds Semantic Kernel and AutoGen, abstracting the
low-level plumbing of agent apps: threaded state, context-provider
memory, middleware for intercepting actions, and typed, graph-based
**workflows** for plan-execute loops and multi-agent orchestration.
[[[Microsoft
Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/semantic-kernel/overview/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}

::: UnorderedList
- **Languages & providers:** Works with **.NET and Python**, with
  built-in support for providers such as **Azure OpenAI/OpenAI** and
  deep integration points for Azure AI. [[[Microsoft
  Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/semantic-kernel/overview/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}.

- **Core capabilities:** Agent **threads** for stateful conversations,
  context providers for memory, **middleware** hooks, **MCP** client
  integration for tools, and workflow features like **conditional
  routing, parallelism, and checkpointing** for long-running,
  human-in-the-loop jobs. [[[Microsoft
  Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/semantic-kernel/overview/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}.

- **Why it exists:** It's the **unified successor** to Semantic Kernel
  and AutoGen, created by the same teams, providing a consistent,
  future-facing API surface. [[[Microsoft Learn+2Microsoft​
  Azure+2]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/semantic-kernel/overview/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}.
:::
::::

[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB80 .pagebreak aria-label="80"
role="doc-pagebreak"}This SDK is geared to solution architects and
backend engineers who want to embed agentic
[patterns]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm24}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm25}
in existing apps, and it pairs cleanly with **Azure AI Agent Service**
when you need a managed, production runtime for threads, identity,
content safety, and observability. [[[Microsoft
Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/semantic-kernel/overview/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}.
:::::

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec7 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec7Heading"}
#### Azure (OpenAI + Cognitive) AI Services/Azure AI Foundry---Models for Language, Vision, Speech, Knowledge {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec7Heading .Heading}

The model catalog [supplies]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm26} the
"brains." Azure OpenAI hosts GPT-4o, Phi-3-mini, and multimodal Vision
models behind enterprise controls ([[[Microsoft
Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/ai-foundry/openai/concepts/models?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef},
[[[Microsoft
Azure]{.RefSource}](https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/ai-services/openai-service?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}),
while Cognitive Services contributes domain APIs for speech, vision,
search, and personalizer.

**Agents can mix-and-match**: call a doc-grounded GPT-4o for reasoning,
then a Neural [text-to-speech
(TTS)]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm27} voice for customer-facing
audio.

This is for data scientists fine-tuning domain-specific LLMs or adding
perception (audio/vision) to existing agents.
:::

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec8 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec8Heading"}
#### Copilot Studio---No-Code Canvas and Fine-Tune Portal {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec8Heading .Heading}

For business makers, [Copilot
Studio]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm28}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm29}
offers a drag-and-drop canvas where you compose dialogs, inject Power
Automate actions, and publish agents to Teams or Dynamics without
writing code ([[[Microsoft
Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/power-platform/release-plan/2025wave1/microsoft-copilot-studio/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef},
[[[Microsoft]{.RefSource}](https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/blog/2025/05/19/introducing-microsoft-365-copilot-tuning-multi-agent-orchestration-and-more-from-microsoft-build-2025/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).

2025 Wave 1 also added **model tuning with enterprise data** and
**multiagent orchestration blocks**---think ReAct loops, but in a
flowchart
([[[Microsoft]{.RefSource}](https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/blog/2025/05/19/introducing-microsoft-365-copilot-tuning-multi-agent-orchestration-and-more-from-microsoft-build-2025/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).

Copilot Studio is also the official canvas for customizing Microsoft 365
Copilot experiences so business users can customize Copilot for M365
without requiring an entire dev project.

This is the best fit for power
[users]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm30}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm31},
product owners, and IT pros who need to prototype quickly and hand
solutions to ops teams.

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par37 .Para}
**How the Layers Click**

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Design** your orchestration plan in Copilot Studio or Microsoft
    Agent Framework.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Deploy** to Azure AI Agent Service for state, memory,
    observability, and enterprise guard-rails.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    []{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB81 .pagebreak aria-label="81"
    role="doc-pagebreak"}**Reason** with Azure OpenAI/Cognitive models;
    stream findings back through the runtime.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

4.  ::: ItemNumber
    4\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Automate** downstream steps via Power Automate or Logic Apps,
    tapping the Fabric lake for fresh data.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

Each tool targets a different
[skill]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm32}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm33}
set yet speaks the same language (OAuth, ARM, OneLake paths), so teams
can **swap parts without starting from scratch every time**. The result
is a cohesive "agent factory" that scales from proof-of-concept chatbots
to mission-critical autonomous workflows.
:::::
:::::::::::::

:::::::::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec9 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec9Heading"}
### [5.1.4 ]{.HeadingNumber}Business Applications Layer (Figure [[5-1](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig1)]{.InternalRef}---Business Applications Circle) {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec9Heading .Heading}

At the summit of the AI [stack]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm34}
sits the [Business Applications
layer]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm35}, where the full strength
and power built at the other layers of the stack coalesce into the daily
workflows of people across your organization.

Whether it's a sales manager spotting an opportunity in Dynamics 365, a
service rep resolving a case through Teams, or a finance analyst
drafting a report in Excel, this layer channels your infrastructure,
data, and AI services into familiar interfaces that amplify productivity
and decision-making.

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec10 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec10Heading"}
#### Dynamics 365 Agents---Embedded Intelligence in Every Role {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec10Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par45 .Para}
Dynamics
[365]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm36}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm37}
provides role-tailored UIs for Sales, Customer Service, Field Service,
Marketing, and more. Behind each screen sits an agentic engine that

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Listens** to real-time business events like new leads, support
    tickets, service calls, and surfaces context-aware suggestions.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Predicts** next steps, for example, identifying upsell signals in
    Sales, recommending KB articles in Service, or forecasting
    maintenance needs in Field Service.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Automates** routine tasks such as logging customer interactions,
    creating follow-up activities, and routing work to the right teams
    without manual handoffs.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::

[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB82 .pagebreak aria-label="82"
role="doc-pagebreak"}
::::
:::::

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec11 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec11Heading"}
#### Power Automate---The Glue That Binds AI to Action {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec11Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par49 .Para}
[Power
Automate]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm38}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm39}
sits alongside Dynamics and Microsoft 365 as the no-code conductor of
your agentic orchestra. It

::: UnorderedList
- **Triggers** on events (a new record in Dataverse, an incoming email,
  a social media mention),

- **Calls** AI services (runs an embedding search, invokes a custom LLM
  with AI Builder or asks a custom Copilot for draft text),

- **Routes** outcomes (creates tasks, updates records, notifies teams in
  Teams or Outlook),

- **Approvals and Human-in-the-Loop** (pauses for sign-off when complex
  judgment is needed).
:::
::::

This seamless handoff
[means]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm40}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm41}
your agents not only think; they intelligently do.
:::::

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec12 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec12Heading"}
#### Copilot for Microsoft 365---An Everyday AI Companion {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec12Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par55 .Para}
Beyond line-of-business
[apps]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm42}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm43},
Copilot for Microsoft 365 brings agentic innovation directly into Office
apps and Teams:

::: UnorderedList
- In **Word**, Copilot can suggest rephrasing and draft executive
  summaries from research.

- In **Excel**, it can build complex macros from a single prompt, write
  Python scripts to perform complex ETLs, and explain anomalies.

- In **PowerPoint**, it can generate slide decks based on real-time
  insights from Word docs, Excel sheets, or Power BI reports.

- In **Teams**, Copilot can act as a real-time facilitator: summarizing
  meeting notes, surfacing action items, and even drafting follow-up
  messages automatically.
:::
::::

This is built for department leaders, analysts, and any knowledge worker
who lives in Microsoft 365 and wants AI to be as ubiquitous as search:
always-on, context-aware, and directly actionable.

In essence, the Business Applications layer is where your agents move
from a "cool toy" to a "reusable asset." It funnels [AI-driven
insights]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm44} and actions into the
familiar []{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB83 .pagebreak aria-label="83"
role="doc-pagebreak"}screens and workflows your teams already use,
making advanced automation and predictive intelligence an invisible but
indispensable part of every role.

What's particularly valuable and unique about the different layers of
the Microsoft AI stack is their level of
[interoperability]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm45}. Microsoft's
tools are designed to work together, ensuring that data can flow freely
across applications, services, and business processes, eliminating silos
and creating a cohesive, integrated experience. This helps minimize
technical debt and, more importantly, drives a fluid business-technology
integration experience.

One key example is the integration between Azure AI and the Power
Platform. For instance, [Power
Automate]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm46} can trigger machine
learning models hosted in Azure to analyze customer interactions or
business data. Once the analysis is complete, Power Automate can
automatically create tasks or trigger workflows based on the results.
This integration enables businesses to automate decision-making
processes, reducing the need for manual input and ensuring that actions
are taken based on real-time data.
:::::
::::::::::::
::::::::::::::::::::::::::

:::::::::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec13 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec13Heading"}
## [5.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Deciding Which Layer to Use {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec13Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par64 .Para}
With so many "agentifying" options like low-code builders, pro-dev
frameworks, managed runtimes, it's easy to get flooded with choices
before you even write your first prompt. Some questions we hear from
teams trying to decide where to begin in the Microsoft AI stack include

::: UnorderedList
- *When do I use AI Builder's pre-built models vs. designing a custom
  flow in Copilot Studio?*

- *Do I first train my own LLM in Azure and then import it into Copilot
  Studio, or can I skip straight to no-code?*

- *If I'm comfortable coding, should I embed agentic patterns with the
  Microsoft Agent Framework SDK, or deploy to the full Azure AI Agent
  Service runtime?*

- *Do I need to hire specialized AI engineers, or can business analysts
  spin up meaningful agents with Power Platform connectors?*

- *Which orchestration tool makes more sense for simple approval flows
  vs. large, event-driven pipelines?*
:::
::::

Choosing the right layer can feel paralyzing, each option offers real
capability, but picking the wrong one can cost time and momentum. To
help you cut through the noise, here are a few field-tested rules of
thumb our clients use to jumpstart their agentic initiatives without
overthinking

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec14 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec14Heading"}
### [5.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Focus on Mapping Where Your Data Lives to Each Tool's Connector Framework {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec14Heading .Heading}

[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB84 .pagebreak aria-label="84"
role="doc-pagebreak"}If you are using
[Dataverse]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm47} and that is the
primary data source, you would waste a lot of engineering effort
connecting it to an agent in Azure when Copilot Studio has native
support for this data source.

If your data lives across APIs with custom schemas, you'll have to spend
most of your budget figuring out how to properly call those APIs with
the right trigger if you try setting this up in Copilot Studio. In
contrast, Azure AI agent service expects OpenAPI specs as part of its
key action list and can update its API understanding with a revised
function signature rather than Copilot Studio which may require an
entire re-work of a particular topic tree.

In essence, by understanding what data your Copilot and/or agent is
going to be [leveraging]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm48} and
identifying whether the complexity of connecting to it is better handled
by connectors in Copilot Studio or Azure AI, you can simplify your
kickoff.
:::

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec15 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec15Heading"}
### [5.2.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Not Every Agent Needs to Interact with a User Through Conversation {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec15Heading .Heading}

[Chat-based AI]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm49} tools like
ChatGPT, Claude, and Microsoft Copilot have trained us to think every
[AI
interaction]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm50}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm51}
must happen through a conversation window. In reality, truly autonomous
agents surface insights and take actions without you ever typing a
prompt. Chat should be an exception, when you need clarification or
handoff, not the default mode of operation.

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par75 .Para}
This is where [**Power Automate**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm52}
and [**Azure Logic Apps**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm53} shine:

::: UnorderedList
- **Event-Driven Triggers**

  Agents listen for business events (new orders, incoming emails, or
  sensor alerts)[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm54} and kick off
  workflows automatically, no user prompt required.

- **Orchestration at Scale**

  Complex, multistep processes (decision trees for claims, automated PO
  approvals, supply-chain replenishment) are defined in visual
  designers, with built-in exception paths and retries.

- [**Human-in-the-Loop (HITL)**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm55}
  **Pauses**

  []{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB85 .pagebreak aria-label="85"
  role="doc-pagebreak"}Flows can automatically hand off to a person when
  judgment is needed, for example, escalating a customer complaint or
  pausing for sign-off on sensitive transactions, then resume
  autonomously once the human approves.

- **Seamless System Integration**

  Hundreds of first-party and third-party connectors let
  [agents]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm56} read data from OneLake
  or Dataverse, call Azure AI models, update CRM records, send
  notifications, and more, all without custom code.
:::
::::

**Example:** An AI [forecasting]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm57}
agent monitors inventory levels in real time. When stock falls below the
threshold, Power Automate automatically creates a replenishment order,
updates the ERP system, and notifies the warehouse manager, no chat
needed until an exception alerts the human.

By embedding agentic logic into your organization's workflow backbone,
you free users from repetitive check-ins, ensure actions happen in real
time, and reserve conversational AI for moments that truly benefit from
human collaboration.
:::::

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec16 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec16Heading"}
### [5.2.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Start at the Top and Drill Deeper {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec16Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par86 .Para}
You aren't locked into a single layer or tool, think of the stack as a
spectrum. Begin with the simplest, highest-level option (Copilot Studio
or Power Automate), then only add lower-level, more complex tooling
(Microsoft Agent Framework, Azure AI Agent Service, custom ML) as your
needs demand.

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par87 .Para}
    [**Kick Off with
    No-Code/Low-Code**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm58}:

    ::: UnorderedList
    - **Copilot Studio**: Build simple agent prototypes, wire up simple
      actions, and publish to Teams or Dynamics in minutes.

    - **Power Automate**: Automate routine tasks and integrate basic AI
      calls (e.g., sentiment analysis, entity extraction) via built-in
      connectors.
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par90 .Para}
    []{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB86 .pagebreak aria-label="86"
    role="doc-pagebreak"}**Validate the
    Concept**[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm59}:

    ::: UnorderedList
    - Test with real users in their daily workflows.

    - Gather feedback on accuracy, speed, and usability.

    - Refine prompts, adjust actions, and tighten guard-rails; all
      without writing a single line of code.
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par94 .Para}
    **Introduce Lightweight Pro-Code when
    needed**[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm60}**:**

    ::: UnorderedList
    - **Microsoft Agent Framework SDK**: When you need custom chaining,
      vector memory, or plan-execute loops, embed small code snippets
      into your existing apps or serverless functions.

    - **Azure Functions**: Encapsulate complex logic or data
      transformations that Power Automate can invoke via HTTP.
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

4.  ::: ItemNumber
    4\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par97 .Para}
    **Scale with** [**Managed Agent
    Runtime**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm61}**:**

    ::: UnorderedList
    - **Azure AI Agent Service**: For mission-critical, stateful agents
      that require full observability, autoscaling, and enterprise
      governance.

    - Swap in custom memory stores (Redis, Cosmos DB) or specialized
      tools without rearchitecting the entire solution.
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

5.  ::: ItemNumber
    5\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par100 .Para}
    **Optimize with** [**Custom ML
    Models**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm62}**:**

    ::: UnorderedList
    - **Azure Machine Learning**: Train/tune domain-specific models when
      off-the-shelf LLMs fall short.

    - Integrate those models back into Copilot Studio or Agent Service
      to boost accuracy on niche tasks.
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

6.  ::: ItemNumber
    6\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par103 .Para}
    [**Iterate and Evolve**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm63}**:**

    ::: UnorderedList
    - Monitor usage and performance via Application Insights and Power
      Platform analytics.

    - Identify bottlenecks or gaps and move deeper into the stack only
      where it adds clear business value, avoiding unnecessary
      complexity elsewhere.
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

By progressing from no-code to pro-code in measured stages, only when
needed, you accelerate time-to-value, minimize risk, and ensure each
layer is only added when it truly unlocks new capabilities.
:::::
::::::::::::

::::::::::::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec17 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec17Heading"}
## [5.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Agentic Framework: Tool Combination Deep Dives {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec17Heading .Heading}

[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB87 .pagebreak aria-label="87"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Having settled on the right entry point and
properly matching scope to tool capabilities, let's walk through some of
the finer details that not only get you started but help you accelerate
your path to success.

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec18 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec18Heading"}
### [5.3.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Implementing Copilot Studio {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec18Heading .Heading}

**Start with a template**[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm64}

As seen in Figure
[[5-2](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig2)]{.InternalRef}, you can open
Copilot [Studio]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm65} and explore the
built-in agent templates: "Website Q&A," "IT Helpdesk," "Benefits
Assistant," and more. A template pre-wires common intents, sample
triggers, and recommended knowledge connections, letting you publish a
working prototype to Teams in minutes. We've watched clients spin up a
personalized Benefits agent this way: they selected the template,
pointed it to HR documents, and had a live bot in Teams in no time.

**No template? Define system message and knowledge first**

<figure id="Fig2" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_MO2" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Fig2_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle3"
alt="Screenshot of the Copilot Studio interface showing the &quot;Explore agents&quot; section with various agent templates. These include &quot;Website Q&amp;A,&quot; &quot;Voice,&quot; &quot;Safe Travels,&quot; &quot;Benefits,&quot; &quot;Citizen Services,&quot; and &quot;Financial Insights,&quot; each with a brief description. Below, the &quot;Learning resources&quot; section lists items like &quot;Free Copilot Studio Workshop,&quot; &quot;Getting started with Copilot Studio,&quot; and &quot;Security and Governance.&quot; The interface is designed for easy navigation and access to resources." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 5-2</span>
<p>Copilot Studio templates: The Copilot Studio home screen highlighting
built-in agent templates (e.g., Website Q&amp;A, Voice, Benefits,
Citizen Services) that jump-start prototyping. Makers can pick a
template, publish to Teams in minutes, and iterate on knowledge sources
and actions</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>

[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB88 .pagebreak aria-label="88"
role="doc-pagebreak"}When you create a blank agent, complete the
**System Message** (role, tone, responsibilities) and **Knowledge
Sources** (SharePoint, web URLs, files, Dataverse)
[tabs]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm66} before anything else. The
system message is the primary data point the agent leverages to
understand its roles, responsibilities, and how it should interact with
its users. The knowledge tab is where you configure data connections to
ensure the agent is answering questions or taking action off of live
information and not using its "best-guess" from its pre-trained memory.

This leads to another [tip]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm67} for
starting; if you're worried about your agent "hallucinating," you have
the option to turn off the agent's general knowledge in the agent
settings. Turning this off means your agent will only use the knowledge
sources you've specified when answering or conducting activities for the
user.

This can be particularly important when you have to be mindful about
connecting your agent to sensitive data sources. If you're an
administrator, you can apply [**Power Platform DLP
policies**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm68}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm69}
in the Admin Center to control *which* knowledge-source connectors an
agent maker can use (SharePoint, web, Azure Blob, SQL, etc.) and even
filter SharePoint endpoints by site to ensure data leakage is
controlled.
:::

:::::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec19 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec19Heading"}
### [5.3.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Azure AI Agent Service Patterns That Will Have You Wiring Agents Together Like A Pro {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec19Heading .Heading}

Let's say you've [outgrown]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm70} the
template phase, you're ready to make some more mature data connections
and create an agent fleet that operates as a business backbone. This is
where you use Azure AI Agent Service as the "control room" that keeps
multiple agents, tools, and memory stores humming in sync.

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec20 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec20Heading"}
#### Start with Model Context Protocol (MCP) {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec20Heading .Heading}

As we know, part of what makes an AI agentic is its ability to call
tools to
[conduct]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm71}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm72}
an action/actions. The main approach to organizing that today is
defining and registering MCP connections.

MCP is simply a structured JSON envelope that travels with every prompt.
In it you declare once which tools the agent can call, what kind of user
or task context to include, and where to read or write memory. Instead
of sprinkling that setup code across half a
[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB89 .pagebreak aria-label="89"
role="doc-pagebreak"}dozen endpoints, you register the profile in the
portal (or via CLI) and point any new agent at it. Need to add a
"GenerateInvoice" tool next quarter? Edit the profile centrally and
every agent
[instantly]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm73}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm74}
knows the new trick.
:::

::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec21 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec21Heading"}
#### Orchestrating Agent-To-Agent (A2A) Handoffs {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec21Heading .Heading}

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par117 .Para}
The moment one
[agent]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm75}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm76}
isn't enough, you have two classic patterns:

::: UnorderedList
- **Sequential**: Imagine a pipeline where a Data-Collector agent
  fetches raw metrics, hands them to an Analyzer, which pushes a summary
  to a Reporter that drafts the email. Each handoff is just the previous
  agent's JSON output.

- **Group-chat**: Sometimes you want three specialists in the same
  virtual "room" brainstorming or voting on a plan. Agent Service keeps
  the thread coherent, tags who said what, and lets you set rules like
  "majority wins" or "fallback to human if they disagree."
:::
::::

Either pattern can be wired to an Event Grid event at key checkpoints,
so Power
[Automate]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm77}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm78}
or Logic Apps can jump in without resorting to ugly polling loops.
:::::

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec22 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec22Heading"}
#### Picking the Right Memory Store {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec22Heading .Heading}

Fast-moving session [state?]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm79} Drop
it into Azure Cache for Redis; sub-millisecond reads keep token-hungry
LLMs happy. Need a long-lived, globally replicated conversation history
or vector search for Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG)? Switch to
Azure Cosmos DB with the vector indexing option turned on. The beauty is
that the agent code doesn't change: you just swap the memory plug-in in
the MCP profile and redeploy.

Put together, these ingredients turn Azure AI Agent Service into your
[production-grade playground]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm80}:
centrally managed context, clean handoffs between agents, and the
freedom to choose the memory that fits the job. Once those pieces click,
you're ready to loop the agent into Power Automate, potentially surface
it in Dynamics, or do anything else your solution demands, confident the
plumbing underneath will keep scale, security, and observability under
control.

Every agent ultimately needs an orchestration "nervous system" and a
place to live inside day-to-day business apps. Power
[Platform]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm81} (with Power Automate,
Dataverse, and Application Insights) supplies the wiring; Dynamics 365
supplies the front-of-house. Below are the core patterns, why they
matter, and how to light them up.
:::
::::::::

::::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec23 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec23Heading"}
### [5.3.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Hardening the Business Applications Layer for AI Success {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec23Heading .Heading}

[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB90 .pagebreak aria-label="90"
role="doc-pagebreak"}Once you've got agents running and orchestration
patterns in place, you'll want to make them *usable, observable, and
safe* where work actually happens. Here's a playbook that ensures AI
shows up reliably in day-to-day workflows: wiring event-driven
automations, sharing agent state, seeing what's happening in production,
and enforcing the right guard-rails.

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec24 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec24Heading"}
#### Power Automate: The Glue (and the Human Brake Pedal) {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec24Heading .Heading}

[Flows]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm82} act as low-code pipelines
that wake up on events like an incoming email, a Dataverse row change,
or a call from an Azure AI Agent, and then fan out actions or approvals.
Approvals, [adaptive-card waits]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm83},
and "Send email with options" all pause the automation until a person
gives the go-ahead ([[[DEV
Community]{.RefSource}](https://dev.to/wyattdave/power-automate-the-power-of-human-in-the-loop-1fp8?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef},
[[[Medium]{.RefSource}](https://medium.com/%2540talhamanzoorpaypal/power-automate-the-power-of-human-in-the-loop-90571a14cf19?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).
This "human-in-the-loop" step is crucial when an autonomous agent is
about to refund a customer or push an urgent change to production.
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec25 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec25Heading"}
#### Dataverse Tables As Shared Memory {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec25Heading .Heading}

Multiple agents (or flows) can post their state into a lightweight
[Dataverse entity]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm84}, think
[AgentRun]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm85} with columns for
Status, Owner, and JSON Payload. Copilot Studio's June 2025 update even
auto-creates these tables when you enable multiagent collaboration,
turning Dataverse into a structured memory hub that every agent can
query or update in real time
([[[Microsoft]{.RefSource}](https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/power-platform/blog/2025/06/16/data-agent-architecture-powered-by-microsoft-dataverse/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec26 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec26Heading"}
#### Application Insights for Deep Telemetry {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec26Heading .Heading}

Turning on [Application Insights]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm86}
for cloud flows streams trigger times, action latencies, and failure
traces into Azure Monitor logs, where you can build proactive alerts or
[Power BI dashboards]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm87}
([[[Microsoft
Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/power-platform/admin/app-insights-cloud-flow?utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).
The same workspace can ingest trace IDs from Azure AI Agent Service,
giving you true end-to-end visibility.
:::

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec27 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec27Heading"}
#### Security Roles and Data-Residency Controls {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec27Heading .Heading}

Your embedded agents inherit the security role of the Application
[User]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm88} you register, so stick to
least-privilege roles and field-level security to prevent over-exposure.
For regulated regions, create local Dataverse environments and lean on
Microsoft's []{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB91 .pagebreak
aria-label="91" role="doc-pagebreak"}[Advanced Data Residency
(ADR)]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm89} plus Copilot privacy
controls to ensure data stays where it should ([[[Microsoft
Learn]{.RefSource}](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/enterprise/m365-dr-workload-copilot?view=o365-worldwide&utm_source=chatgpt.com)]{.ExternalRef}).

In essence, use [Power Automate]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm90}
to stitch agents, data, and humans together; log everything with
Application Insights; store shared state in Dataverse. Then surface the
intelligence right where work happens, inside Dynamics 365 pages that
respect the same security roles and residency rules your organization
already lives by.

No matter where you're jumping in from, re-visit these tips and
Microsoft's implementation resources, like the Copilot Studio
Implementation Guide, to consolidate your path to success so you don't
feel like you're walking into the unknown blind.
:::
:::::::
:::::::::::::::

::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec28 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec28Heading"}
## [5.4 ]{.HeadingNumber}Success Stories and Real World Applications {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Sec28Heading .Heading}

Now that we've explored the ins and outs of navigating and leveraging
the Microsoft AI stack effectively, we can step out of the workshop and
into live deployments to illustrate how putting all these concepts
together could look like for you in real life.

**Case Study 1:** [**Autonomous Field Operations
Agent**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm91}

A mid-sized industrial client was already logging every incident, form
task, hazard report, and observation in Dataverse. Each morning, their
operations team spent crucial hours manually extracting that data,
aggregating metrics, and drafting analysis for the daily shift-start
meeting. This reactive process meant they were always playing catch-up
rather than proactively guiding the day's priorities.

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par134 .Para}
We built an overnight, fully automated agentic workflow using Power
Automate and AI Builder, transforming their Dataverse records into a
polished daily [briefing]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm92} without
any human intervention.

<figure id="Fig3" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_MO3" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Fig3_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle3"
alt="Flow chart illustrating a process involving Power Automate, Dataverse, and AI Builder Prompt. Power Automate feeds into Dataverse, which connects to three data tables: Incidents, Form Tasks, and Hazards &amp; Observations. Dataverse also links to AI Builder Prompt, leading to a Daily Form Summary. This summary is sent to a Leadership Blast and a Company Collaboration Tool. Numbered circles (1, 2, 3) are present but not explained." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 5-3</span>
<p>Autonomous daily briefing (field operations): Power Automate pulls
incidents, tasks, and hazards from Dataverse, sends them to an AI
Builder prompt to generate a “Daily Form Summary,” then distributes it
automatically. The briefing lands in leaders’ inboxes and the team’s
collaboration space; no chat required</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par135 .Para}
::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par136 .Para}
    []{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB92 .pagebreak aria-label="92"
    role="doc-pagebreak"}**Data Ingestion and
    Trigger**[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm93} **(Figure**
    [[**5-3**](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig3)]{.InternalRef}**---Part
    1)**

    ::: UnorderedList
    - A scheduled Power Automate
      [flow]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm94} ran at 2 AM local
      time, querying the Dataverse tables for new incidents, form tasks,
      hazards, and observations from the previous 24 hours.
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par138 .Para}
    **Analysis and Narration (Figure**
    [[**5-3**](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig3)]{.InternalRef}**---Part
    2)**

    ::: UnorderedList
    - The flow passed those records to an AI Builder text-generation
      model, which was configured with a lightweight prompt template:
      "Summarize X new incidents and Y form tasks, highlighting top
      three hazards and trends." This avoided heavyweight LLM
      fine-tuning or custom infrastructure.
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::::: ItemContent
    :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par140 .Para}
    **Delivery and Integration (Figure**
    [[**5-3**](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig3)]{.InternalRef}**---Part
    3)**

    ::: UnorderedList
    - :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par141 .Para}
      The generated [summary]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm95} was
      posted into two places
      simultaneously:[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB93 .pagebreak
      aria-label="93" role="doc-pagebreak"}

      ::: UnorderedList
      - A daily meeting note auto-created in the company's collaboration
        tool.

      - An email digest sent to all shift leads before the first team
        arrived on site.
      :::
      ::::
    :::
    ::::
    :::::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par144 .Para}
**Why This Layer and Toolset**

::: UnorderedList
- Power Automate proved ideal for connecting to Dataverse and scheduling
  data pulls.

- AI Builder delivered a no-code path to embed LLM-style summaries
  without data-science overhead, keeping technical debt low.

- This pattern fit perfectly at the Business Applications layer: the
  team never had to "chat" with the agent, it simply ran in the
  background, surfacing insights where work already happened.
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par148 .Para}
**Outcomes and Impact**

::: UnorderedList
- Operations [leads]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm96} reclaimed
  1--2 hours each morning, shifting from data prep to decision-making.

- Teams began their shifts armed with prioritized action items, not
  scrambling to assemble reports.

- The solution launched in under a month, required no developer
  headcount, and now runs with zero maintenance.
:::
::::

This use case exemplifies our "start at the top and drill deeper"
heuristic. By beginning with low-code Power Automate and AI Builder, the
client rapidly proved value, then consolidated their agent into existing
business apps, turning a repetitive "cool toy" into a reusable
operational asset. It also underscores our "no chat required" rule,
showing that truly autonomous agents can deliver high-impact insights
without a single conversational prompt.

**Case Study 2: Real-Time Data Agent for Real Estate Investment Trusts**

A large Real Estate Investment Trust
[(REIT)]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm97}[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm98}
client managed a fast-moving portfolio of properties, leases, and
maintenance records in an Azure SQL-backed data product. They also ran
Azure Document Intelligence to OCR lease documents and expense invoices.
Yet every ad hoc query, whether "What's the current occupancy rate in
Building A?" or "Show me expense trends for Q2," required analysts to
switch between SQL dashboards, custom BI tools, and the Document
Intelligence portal. This fractured workflow slowed decision-making and
made real-time insights feel like a luxury.

::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par155 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB94 .pagebreak aria-label="94"
role="doc-pagebreak"}We built an interactive, conversational agent on
[Azure AI Agent Service]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm99} combined
with Azure OpenAI, Azure Functions, and Azure Document Intelligence to
give non-technical users instant, real-time access and update
capabilities, all from a single chat interface embedded in their
investment console.

<figure id="Fig4" class="Figure">
<div id="662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_MO4" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Fig4_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle18"
alt="Flow chart illustrating a user-agent interaction process. The user sends a message to an agent via an Azure Web App. The AI agent interprets the message and interacts with Azure AI Agent Service. The service connects to Azure Cosmos DB, Azure Function App, and Azure SQL Database. It also performs AI OCR operations using Azure AI Document Intelligence and Azure Blob Storage. The agent replies with the requested information. Arrows indicate the flow of data and interactions between components." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 5-4</span>
<p>Real-time REIT <span
id="662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm100">agent</span> on Azure: A web
app fronts an AI agent hosted on Azure AI Agent Service, which calls
Azure Functions to query Azure SQL and run Azure AI Document
Intelligence on files in Blob Storage. Conversation state and audit logs
persist in Azure Cosmos DB, and responses return to the user through a
single chat experience</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>
:::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par156 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB95 .pagebreak aria-label="95"
role="doc-pagebreak"}What you're seeing in Figure
[[5-4](#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Fig4)]{.InternalRef}:

::: UnorderedList
- :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par157 .Para}
  [**Dynamic Data Retrieval**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm101}

  ::: UnorderedList
  - The agent uses Azure AI Agent Service to parse user intents (e.g.,
    "Show me February occupancy by unit type").

  - Via MCP-registered tools, it invokes an Azure Function that queries
    the Azure SQL database with parameterized T-SQL, ensuring
    up-to-the-minute results.
  :::
  ::::

- :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par160 .Para}
  [**On-Demand Document
  Insights**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm102}

  ::: UnorderedList
  - When users ask about lease terms or invoice line-items, the agent
    can call the Azure Document Intelligence endpoint to OCR the latest
    PDFs stored in Azure Blob Storage.

  - Extracted fields flow back through the same function pipeline,
    merging structured data with unstructured text for a unified answer.
  :::
  ::::

- :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par163 .Para}
  [**Live Updates and
  Transactions**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm103}

  ::: UnorderedList
  - Beyond read queries, the agent can submit updates, such as marking a
    lease renewal or flagging an expense exception, by invoking secured
    stored procedures via the Azure Function tool.

  - All actions are captured in Azure Cosmos DB as agent transaction
    logs for auditability and downstream analytics.
  :::
  ::::

- :::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par166 .Para}
  [**Unified Interaction
  Console**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm104}

  ::: UnorderedList
  - We embedded the agent in a custom web portal built on Azure Web
    Apps, so users never leave their investment dashboard.

  - The chat [interface]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm105}
    dynamically adapts to user roles (analyst vs. asset manager),
    showing only the permitted operations and data scopes.
  :::
  ::::
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par169 .Para}
**Why This Layer and Toolset**

::: UnorderedList
- Azure AI Agent [Service]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm106}
  provided the scalable, stateful runtime and integrated MCP for tool
  orchestration.

- []{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB96 .pagebreak aria-label="96"
  role="doc-pagebreak"}Azure Functions offered a secure, serverless
  bridge to both Azure SQL and Document Intelligence APIs.

- Azure OpenAI delivered natural-language understanding and generation
  without building a custom model.

- This pattern sat squarely in the AI Service Suite and Infrastructure
  Foundation layer, leveraging existing Azure investments for rapid
  delivery.
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par174 .Para}
[**Outcomes and Impact**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm107}

::: UnorderedList
- Analysts received answers in seconds instead of spending 10--15
  minutes navigating multiple tools.

- 100% of data interactions, read and write, occur within a single,
  role-aware chat console.

- Adoption soared across business units as the agent removed technical
  barriers to data.

- All agent transactions are logged in Cosmos DB, satisfying internal
  controls without extra dev work.
:::
::::

It also highlights our "[Toolbox
Spectrum]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm108}" tip: rather than
shoehorning into Copilot Studio or Power Automate, we matched the agent
runtime to the client's existing Azure ecosystem, delivering a tailored,
real-time solution that scales with their data velocity.

[**Leadership Checklist**]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm109}**:
Navigating Microsoft's AI Stack**

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par181 .Para}
![A black check mark symbol inside a square with rounded
corners.](images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Figa_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
**Map Your Data Sources**

::: UnorderedList
- Inventory where your critical data lives (Dataverse, OneLake, Azure
  SQL, external APIs).

- Align each source to the tool with native connectors (e.g., Copilot
  Studio for Dataverse; Azure AI Agent Service + Azure Functions for
  custom APIs).
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par184 .Para}
![A black check mark symbol inside a square with rounded
corners.](images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Figb_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
**Choose the Right Entry Point**

::: UnorderedList
- **Rapid Prototype**: Use Copilot Studio or Power Automate for low-code
  proofs of concept.

- **Scale and Control**: Deploy Azure AI Agent Service with MCP for
  production-grade orchestration and enterprise governance.
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par187 .Para}
[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_PB97 .pagebreak aria-label="97"
role="doc-pagebreak"}![A black check mark inside a square box,
symbolizing approval or
completion.](images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Figc_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
**Balance Autonomy and Oversight**

::: UnorderedList
- Embed fully [autonomous]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm110} agents
  for routine, event-driven insights (no chat required).

- Reserve chat interfaces for exceptions, clarifications, or
  human-in-the-loop sign-offs.
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par190 .Para}
![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing approval or
completion. The check mark is centered and prominent, with a thick black
outline against a white
background.](images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Figd_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}
**Govern Data and Knowledge Flows**

::: UnorderedList
- Apply DLP policies in the Power Platform Admin Center to restrict
  connectors and control sensitive data movement.

- Leverage Advanced Data Residency (ADR), private endpoints, and
  role-based access in Copilot and Dynamics.
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par193 .Para}
![A bold check mark symbol inside a square box, representing
confirmation or approval. The check mark is centered and prominent
within the
box.](images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Fige_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}**Monitor,
Measure, and Iterate**

::: UnorderedList
- Track workflows with
  [Application]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm111} Insights and
  Azure Monitor for full observability.

- Analyze adoption metrics, response times, and error rates; refine
  prompts, guardrails, and memory stores as usage scales.
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par196 .Para}
![A black check mark symbol inside a square with rounded
corners.](images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Figf_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}**Embed
Into Business Applications**

::: UnorderedList
- **Surface insights directly where work happens**: Dynamics 365, Teams,
  Excel, and Power Apps.

- Use Canvas Apps or Custom Pages in Dynamics for pixel-perfect agent
  panels and secure, role-based integration.
:::
::::

:::: {#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_Par199 .Para}
![A checkmark symbol inside a square box, indicating a selection or
confirmation.](images/662753_1_En_5_Chapter/662753_1_En_5_Figg_HTML.gif){.ImageStyle17}**Plan
for Next-Level Maturity**

::: UnorderedList
- Identify where low-code
  [proofs]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm112} can graduate to
  pro-dev patterns using Microsoft Agent Framework or custom ML in Azure
  Machine Learning.

- Schedule periodic reviews to evolve from single agents to orchestrated
  multiagent systems and cross-department automation.
:::
::::

*Will leans back, tapping the final node in the boardroom diagram.
"We've seen how every layer, from OneLake to Copilot to Dynamics, plays
its part. The engines are humming."*

*Nancie nods. "Our teams are more proactive than ever. But with great
power comes great responsibility. We need guard-rails as robust as our
pipelines."*

*Cal's agent icon pulses*[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm113} *on
the screen. "Shall I generate a compliance report summarizing our data
flows, access logs, and model-drift alerts?"*

*Will smiles. "Just what we need. Let's make sure our agents stay
trustworthy and transparent as they grow more capable."*

*Nancie taps her tablet. "On to Chapter*
[[[*6*]{.RefSource}](#662753_1_En_6_Chapter.xhtml)]{.ExternalRef}*:
building those guard-rails, bias checks, audit trails, and governance
patterns that keep our agents*[]{#662753_1_En_5_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm114}
*aligned with both business goals and ethical standards."*

*Cal responds, "Initializing Responsible AI framework template, ready
when you are."*
